                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">α-NaFeO2: ionic conductivity and sodium extraction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Blesa, M.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Complex admittance measurements have been performed on α-NaFeO2 and on the product Na0.9FeO2 obtained by sodium extn., both being polycryst. powders.  The elec. cond. in both samples is proposed to be due to sodium ions hopping between octahedral positions through the adjacent, empty, tetrahedral ones characteristic of a rock-salt structural framework.  The parent material shows an activation energy in the d.c. cond. of 0.31 eV between 306 and 498 K.  Removal of sodium, in spite of creating octahedral vacancies, results in lower cond. values, and a higher activation energy of 0.58 eV in a similar temp. range.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrNx6t7nnuGdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgJPtlvXS9gCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3cXhtVajsrw%253D&amp;md5=4d7b27b8f61e3790836bed3f60ca1d49</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1021/jp5105888"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ikeuchi, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nakayama, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Takei, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shiiba, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nakayama, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">New Insight into Structural Evolution in Layered NaCrO<sub>2</sub> during Electrochemical Sodium Extraction</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New Insight into Structural Evolution in Layered NaCrO2 during Electrochemical Sodium Extraction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kubota, Kei; Ikeuchi, Issei; Nakayama, Tetsuri; Takei, Chikara; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Shiiba, Hiromasa; Nakayama, Masanobu; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">119</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">166-175</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. properties and structural changes during charge for NaCrO2, whose structure is classified as α-NaFeO2 type layered polymorph (also O3-type following the Delmas' notation), were examd. as a pos. electrode material for nonaq. Na-ion batteries.  NaCrO2 delivers initial discharge capacity of 110 mAh g-1 at 1/20 C rate in the voltage range of 2.5-3.6 V based on reversible Cr3+/Cr4+ redox without oxidn. to hexavalent Cr ions, while the initial discharge capacity is only 9 mAh g-1 when cutoff voltage is set to 4.5 V.  Results from ex-situ x-ray diffraction, X-ray absorption spectroscopy, and DFT calcns. reveal that the irreversible phase transition occurs after Na extn. by charging over a voltage plateau at 3.8 V assocd. with the lattice shrinkage along the c-axis in the case of x &gt; 0.5 in Na1-xCrO2, which originates from the migration of Cr ions from octahedral sites in CrO2 slabs to both tetrahedral and octahedral sites in interslab layer.  The irreversible structural change would disturb Na insertion into the damaged layer structure during discharge, resulting in the loss of reversibility as electrode materials.  Reversible cycle range with stable capacity retention is, therefore, limited to the compositional range of 0.0 ≤ x ≤ 0.5 in Na1-xCrO2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqs4AHWSSBMyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgJPtlvXS9gCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVCls7rO&amp;md5=a2e967016700fa8b6f0c6ea16b232062</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1039/C3CC49856E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yoshida, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ikeuchi, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Garsuch, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Schulz-Dobrick, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">P2-type Na<sub>2/3</sub>Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as a new positive electrode for higher energy Na-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anomalous Jahn-Teller behavior in a manganese-based mixed-phosphate cathode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hyungsub; Yoon, Gabin; Park, Inchul; Park, Kyu-Young; Lee, Byungju; Kim, Jongsoon; Park, Young-Uk; Jung, Sung-Kyun; Lim, Hee-Dae; Ahn, Docheon; Lee, Seongsu; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3325-3335</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a 3.8 V manganese-based mixed-phosphate cathode material for applications in sodium rechargeable batteries; i.e., Na4Mn3(PO4)2(P2O7).  This material exhibits a largest Mn2+/Mn3+ redox potential of 3.84 V vs.  Na+/Na yet reported for a manganese-based cathode, together with the largest energy d. of 416 W h kg-1.  We describe first-principles calcns. and exptl. results which show that three-dimensional Na diffusion pathways with low-activation-energy barriers enable the rapid sodium insertion and extn. at various states of charge of the Na4-xMn3(PO4)2(P2O7) electrode (where x = 0, 1, 3).  Furthermore, we show that the sodium ion mobility in this crystal structure is not decreased by the structural changes induced by Jahn-Teller distortion (Mn3+), in contrast to most manganese-based electrodes, rather it is increased due to distortion, which opens up sodium diffusion channels.  This feature stabilizes the material, providing high cycle stability and high power performance for sodium rechargeable batteries.  The high voltage, large energy d., cycle stability and the use of low-cost Mn give Na4Mn3(PO4)2(P2O7) significant potential for applications as a cathode material for large-scale Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqkGCBDNIeK6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lizKQe71J2-ag"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFWhtL%252FE&amp;md5=627f366282ae7d72c11a642edc8e90d4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201402095"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Barpanda, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, G.-D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Maxim, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamada, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">t-Na2(VO)P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>: A 3.8 V Pyrophosphate Insertion Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ChemElectroChem</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">1</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1488</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1491</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Role of intermediate phase for stable cycling of Na7V4(P2O7)4PO4 in sodium ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lim, Soo Yeon; Kim, Heejin; Chung, Jaehoon; Lee, Ji Hoon; Kim, Byung Gon; Choi, Jeon-Jin; Chung, Kyung Yoon; Cho, Woosuk; Kim, Seung-Joo; Goddard, William A., III; Jung, Yousung; Choi, Jang Wook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States of America</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">111</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">599-604</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0027-8424</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">National Academy of Sciences</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries offer promising opportunities in emerging utility grid applications because of the low cost of raw materials, yet low energy d. and limited cycle life remain crit. drawbacks in their electrochem. operations.  Herein, we report a vanadium-based ortho-diphosphate, Na7V4(P2O7)4PO4 (VODP), that significantly reduces all these drawbacks.  Indeed, VODP exhibits single-valued voltage plateaus at 3.88 V vs. Na/Na+ while retaining substantial capacity (&gt;78%) over 1000 cycles.  Electronic structure calcns. show that the remarkable single plateau and cycle life originate from an intermediate phase (a very shallow voltage step) that is similar both in the energy level and lattice parameters to those of fully intercalated and deintercalated states.  We propose a theor. scheme in which the reaction barrier that arises from lattice mismatches can be evaluated by using a simple energetic consideration, suggesting that the presence of intermediate phases is beneficial for cell kinetics by buffering the differences in lattice parameters between initial and final phases.  We expect these insights into the role of intermediate phases found for VODP hold in general and thus provide a helpful guideline in the further understanding and design of battery materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqaiNxbq_X8WbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lizKQe71J2-ag"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXotFeqtw%253D%253D&amp;md5=284b0140d7ba81f96b846de230711d82</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.01.162"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nose, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nakayama, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nobuhara, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamaguchi, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nakanishi, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Iba, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sub>4</sub>Co<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>: A novel storage material for sodium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Power Sources</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">234</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">175</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">179</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.01.162</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D234%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D175-179%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DM.%2BNose%26author%3DH.%2BNakayama%26author%3DK.%2BNobuhara%26author%3DH.%2BYamaguchi%26author%3DS.%2BNakanishi%26author%3DH.%2BIba%26title%3DNa4Co3%2528PO4%25292P2O7%253A%2BA%2Bnovel%2Bstorage%2Bmaterial%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2013.01.162&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b13516&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2013.01.162&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7: A novel storage material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nose, Masafumi; Nakayama, Hideki; Nobuhara, Kunihiro; Yamaguchi, Hiroyuki; Nakanishi, Shinji; Iba, Hideki</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">234</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">175-179</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 as a pos. electrode for sodium-ion batteries were characterized by a cyclic voltammetry technique and galvanostatic charge/discharge tests.  Interestingly, Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 has the multi-redox couples in the highest potential region between 4.1 V and 4.7 V among ever reported sodium storage materials and can deliver the reversible capacity of ∼95 mAhg-1, corresponding to ∼2.2 Na+ extn. and insertion in Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7, at the c.d. of 34 mAg-1 (0.2 C).  Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 also exhibits the high rate capabilities and has a small polarization in the charge-discharge profile even at the high current densities of 4.25 Ag-1 (25 C), resulting in high energy efficiency of the battery.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The rapid consumption of nonrenewable resources resulted in an ever-increasing problem of CO2 emissions that has motivated people for studying the harvesting of energy from renewable alternatives (e.g. solar and wind).  Efficient electrochem. energy storage devices play a crucial role in storing harvested energies in the daily lives.  For example, rechargeable batteries can store energy generated by solar cells during the daytime and release it during night-time.  In particular, Li-ion batteries (LIBs) have received considerable attention ever since their early commercialization in 1990s.  However, with initiatives by several governments to build large-scale energy grids to store energy for cities, problems such as the high cost and limited availability of Li starts to become major issues.  Na, which also belongs to Group 1 of the periodic table, has comparable electrochem. properties to Li, and more importantly it is considerably more accessible than Li.  Nonetheless, research into Na-ion batteries (NIBs) is currently still in its infancy compared to LIBs, although great leaps and bounds have been made recently in terms of research and development into this technol.  Here in this review, the authors summarize the recent advancements made, also covering the prospective materials for both the battery cathode and anode.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na2FeP2O7: A Safe Cathode for Rechargeable Sodium-ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Barpanda, Prabeer; Liu, Guandong; Ling, Chris D.; Tamaru, Mao; Avdeev, Maxim; Chung, Sai-Cheong; Yamada, Yuki; Yamada, Atsuo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Vying for newer sodium-ion chem. for rechargeable batteries, Na2FeP2O7 pyrophosphate has been recently unveiled as a 3 V high-rate cathode.  In addn. to its low cost and promising electrochem. performance, here we demonstrate Na2FeP2O7 as a safe cathode with high thermal stability.  Chem./electrochem. desodiation of this insertion compd. has led to the discovery of a new polymorph of NaFeP2O7.  High-temp. analyses of the desodiated state NaFeP2O7 show an irreversible phase transition from triclinic (P‾1) to the ground state monoclinic (P21/c) polymorph above 560°. This high operational stability is rooted in the stable pyrophosphate (P2O7)4- anion, which offers better safety than other phosphate-based cathodes.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na2FeP2O7 as a Promising Iron-Based Pyrophosphate Cathode for Sodium Rechargeable Batteries: A Combined Experimental and Theoretical Study</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Heejin; Shakoor, R. A.; Park, Chansun; Lim, Soo Yeon; Kim, Joo-Seong; Jo, Yong Nam; Cho, Woosuk; Miyasaka, Keiichi; Kahraman, Ramazan; Jung, Yousung; Choi, Jang Wook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering the promising electrochem. performance of the recently reported pyrophosphate family in Li ion batteries as well as the increasing importance of Na ion batteries (SIBs) for emerging large-scale applications, here, the crystal structure, electrochem. properties, and thermal stability of Na2FeP2O7, the 1st example ever reported in the pyrophosphate family for SIBs, are studied.  Na2FeP2O7 maintains well-defined channel structures (triclinic framework under the P1 space group) and exhibits a reversible capacity of ≈90 mA-h g-1 with good cycling performance.  Both quasi-equil. measurements and 1st-principles calcns. consistently indicate that Na2FeP2O7 undergoes 2 kinds of reactions over the entire voltage range of 2.0-4.5 V (vs. Na/Na+): a single-phase reaction around 2.5 V and 2-phase reactions in the voltage range of 3.0-3.25 V.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sol-gel synthesis of Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7)/C nanocomposite for sodium ion batteries and new insights into microstructural evolution during sodium extraction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xuehang; Zhong, Guiming; Tang, Zheng; Yang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">327</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">666-674</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A mixed polyanionic Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7)/C nanocomposite is synthesized via a sol-gel route.  The phosphate raw material is transformed to the mixed phosphate-pyrophosphate with high phase purity via a self-condensation reaction at 500°.  Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7)/C can deliver an initial capacity of 110 mAh g-1 at 0.05C with the av. discharge voltage approaching 3.1 V.  The nanocomposite shows excellent rate capability because of the presence of an in-situ formed 3-D network of carbon.  At 10 C rate, the nanocomposite delivers a discharge capacity of 78 mAh g-1 at 25 mAh °C and 82 mAh g-1 at 55°.  The nanocomposite has a good long-term cycling stability, retaining 89% of the initial discharge capacity after 300 cycles.  In-situ XRD results demonstrate that the sodium insertion/extn. process in Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) is an imperfect solid-soln. reaction with an obvious local lattice distortion instead of an ideal solid-soln. reaction.  Using a solid-state NMR technique, it is further found that the sodium extn. from the Na1, Na3, and Na4 sites causes an obvious change in local structure.  However, the local structure of Na2 remains unchanged, which may aid the stability of the host structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqmFFHRy3nSX7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0limh0im-Tz62A"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the Electrochemical Mechanism of the New Iron-Based Mixed-Phosphate Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) in a Na Rechargeable Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hyungsub; Park, Inchul; Lee, Seongsu; Kim, Hyunchul; Park, Kyu-Young; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Haegyeom; Kim, Jongsoon; Lim, Hee-Dae; Yoon, Won-Sub; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3614-3622</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Compds. with a mixed polyanion framework have recently gained attention as a new class of compds. for material exploration.  The potential tunability of the structure by using various combinations of polyanions can potentially lead to a novel cathode.  However, the redox reaction in complex structures often involves complex structural evolutions during the electrochem. reaction, which require careful anal.  The authors studied the electrochem. mechanism of NaxFe3(PO4)2(P2O7) (1 ≤ x ≤ 4), which was recently proposed as a promising mixed-polyanion cathode for Na rechargeable batteries, using 1st principles calcns. and expts.  The de/sodiation of the NaxFe3(PO4)2(P2O7) electrode occurs via a 1-phase reaction with a reversible Fe2+/Fe3+ redox reaction and accompanies an exceptionally small volumetric change of &lt;4%.  Na ion intercalation usually induces a large volumetric change in conventional systems; therefore, this small vol. change is unusual and was attributed to the open framework of polyanion compds. with P2O7 dimers that are capable of rotating and distorting to accommodate the structural change.  Structural robustness was further obsd. at even highly charged states at temps. ≤530° from in situ XRD and DSC.  Probably the improved understanding of the electrochem. mechanism provided here will expedite the optimization of the new Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) electrode for Na rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr1_81hmtAC77Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0limh0im-Tz62A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXht1KltLnP&amp;md5=96dcd039c0826d84e3fab365efdbb041</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5358"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Barpanda, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oyama, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nishimura, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chung, S.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamada, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A 3.8-V earth-abundant sodium battery electrode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A 3.8-V earth-abundant sodium battery electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Barpanda, Prabeer; Oyama, Gosuke; Nishimura, Shin-ichi; Chung, Sai-Cheong; Yamada, Atsuo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4358</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable lithium batteries have ushered the wireless revolution over last two decades and are now matured to enable green automobiles.  However, the growing concern on scarcity and large-scale applications of lithium resources have steered effort to realize sustainable sodium-ion batteries, Na and Fe being abundant and low-cost charge carrier and redox center, resp.  However, their performance is limited owing to low operating voltage and sluggish kinetics.  Here we report a hitherto-unknown material with entirely new compn. and structure with the first alluaudite-type sulfate framework, Na2Fe2(SO4)3, registering the highest-ever Fe3+/Fe2+ redox potential at 3.8 V (vs. Na, and hence 4.1 V vs. Li) along with fast rate kinetics.  Rare-metal-free Na-ion rechargeable battery system compatible with the present Li-ion battery is now in realistic scope without sacrificing high energy d. and high power, and paves way for discovery of new earth-abundant sustainable cathodes for large-scale batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_sUr2Jpgw1LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbJ6I_Gs5AMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVShs77L&amp;md5=20951f27b1483820983947a5d84d607f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta10210f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Barpanda, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ye, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Avdeev, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chung, S.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamada, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A new polymorph of Na<sub>2</sub>MnP<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub> as a 3.6 V cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A new polymorph of Na2MnP2O7 as a 3.6 V cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Barpanda, Prabeer; Ye, Tian; Avdeev, Maxim; Chung, Sai-Cheong; Yamada, Atsuo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4194-4197</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploring novel low-cost cathodes for sodium-ion batteries, here we unveil β-Na2MnP2O7, a new pyrophosphate cathode.  Stabilizing into a triclinic structure, it was found to be electrochem. active, delivering a discharge capacity approaching 80 mA-h/g along with the highest ever Mn3+/Mn2+ redox potential located at 3.6 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJv7H2f_s1i7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbJ6I_Gs5AMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXjs1ems7c%253D&amp;md5=06ceeb77b0da82843238f8973595a9ca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1021/ja312044k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, C.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shakoor, R.-A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lim, S.-Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kahraman, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, J. W.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anomalous Manganese Activation of a Pyrophosphate Cathode in Sodium Ion Batteries: A Combined Experimental and Theoretical Study</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Am. Chem. Soc.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">135</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2787</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">92</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja312044k</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D135%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D2787-92%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DC.-S.%2BPark%26author%3DH.%2BKim%26author%3DR.-A.%2BShakoor%26author%3DE.%2BYang%26author%3DS.-Y.%2BLim%26author%3DR.%2BKahraman%26author%3DY.%2BJung%26author%3DJ.%2BW.%2BChoi%26title%3DAnomalous%2BManganese%2BActivation%2Bof%2Ba%2BPyrophosphate%2BCathode%2Bin%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%253A%2BA%2BCombined%2BExperimental%2Band%2BTheoretical%2BStudy%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fja312044k&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b13516&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fja312044k&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anomalous manganese activation of a pyrophosphate cathode in sodium in batteries: a combined experimental and theoretical study</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Chan Sun; Kim, Heejin; Shakoor, Rana A.; Yang, Eunjeong; Lim, Soo Yeon; Kahraman, Ramazan; Jung, Yousung; Choi, Jang Wook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">135</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2787-2792</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have many advantages such as the low price and abundance of sodium raw materials that are suitable for large-scale energy storage applications.  Herein, we report an Mn-based pyrophosphate, Na2MnP2O7, as a new SIB cathode material.  Unlike most Mn-based cathode materials, which suffer severely from sluggish kinetics, Na2MnP2O7 exhibits good electrochem. activity at ∼3.8 V vs Na/Na+ with a reversible capacity of 90 mAh g-1 at room temp.  It also shows an excellent cycling and rate performance: 96% capacity retention after 30 cycles and 70% capacity retention at a c-rate increase from 0.05C to 1C.  These electrochem. activities of the Mn-contg. cathode material even at room temp. with relatively large particle sizes are remarkable considering an almost complete inactivity of the Li counterpart, Li2MnP2O7.  Using first-principles calcns., we find that the significantly enhanced kinetics of Na2MnP2O7 is mainly due to the locally flexible accommodation of Jahn-Teller distortions aided by the corner-sharing crystal structure in triclinic Na2MnP2O7.  By contrast, in monoclinic Li2MnP2O7, the edge-sharing geometry causes multiple bonds to be broken and formed during charging reaction with a large degree of at. rearrangements.  We expect that the similar computational strategy to analyze the at. rearrangements can be used to predict the kinetics behavior when exploring new cathode candidates.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCVsDHC4SLQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbJ6I_Gs5AMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFejs74%253D&amp;md5=dd14f197ad7ab2f90e1e95d54c8c8dfa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA01946G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Feng, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kangli, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shijie, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kai, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4)3</sub>/C synthesized by a facile solid-phase method assisted with agarose as a highperformance cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">10261</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">10268</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C7TA01946G</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D10261-10268%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DP.%2BFeng%26author%3DW.%2BWei%26author%3DW.%2BKangli%26author%3DC.%2BShijie%26author%3DJ.%2BKai%26title%3DNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%252FC%2Bsynthesized%2Bby%2Ba%2Bfacile%2Bsolid-phase%2Bmethod%2Bassisted%2Bwith%2Bagarose%2Bas%2Ba%2Bhighperformance%2Bcathode%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC7TA01946G&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b13516&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC7TA01946G&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2(PO4)3/C synthesized by a facile solid-phase method assisted with agarose as a high-performance cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Pingyuan; Wang, Wei; Wang, Kangli; Cheng, Shijie; Jiang, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10261-10268</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A type of Na3V2(PO4)3/C (NVP/C) cathode material for sodium ion batteries was synthesized via a facile solid-phase method.  Agarose, a natural polysaccharide from seaweed that can form a 3D network structure through hydrogen bonds in polar solvents, was used as a carbon source and a medium to form NVP/C particles as nanograins with a thin layer of carbon coating in a 3D carbon network.  As the cathode, the NVP/C material exhibited a reversible capacity of 116 mA h g-1 at 1C, which is very close to its theor. capacity (117.6 mA h g-1), with a capacity retention of 97.3% after 500 cycles.  At 20C, the NVP/C had a capacity of 100 mA h g-1 and still kept a relatively stable capacity of 78 mA h g-1 after being cycled 7000 times.  Based on the excellent performance of the obtained cathode material, a sodium ion full cell was assembled with S-doped carbon as the anode, which delivered 110 mA h g-1 of discharge capacity at 200 mA h g-1 (calcd. using NVP as the cathode) and displayed an av. voltage of around 1.7 V.  All of these results imply that the prepd. NVP/C has potential for application in sodium ion batteries for large-scale energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrio6YwlCOvtrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbJ6I_Gs5AMA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">A new polyanion-based compd., Na3.12M2.44(P2O7)2 (M = Fe, Fe0.5Mn0.5, Mn) is synthesized and examd. as a cathode for Na ion batteries.  Off-stoichiometric synthesis induces the formation of a Na-rich phase, Na3.32Fe2.34(P2O7)2 - a member of the solid soln. series Na4-αFe2+α/2(P2O7)2 (2/3 ≤ α ≤ 7/8) - which delivers a reversible capacity of about 85 mA h g-1 at ca. 3 V vs. Na/Na+ and exhibits very stable cycle performance.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2/multi-walled carbon nanotube composite as a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Niu, Yubin; Xu, Maowen; Cheng, Chuanjun; Bao, ShuJuan; Hou, Junke; Liu, Sangui; Yi, Fenglian; He, Hong; Li, Chang Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2/multi-walled carbon nanotube (MWCNT) composite was fabricated by a solid state reaction and was further used to fabricate a cathode for sodium-ion batteries.  The electrochem. behaviors were thoroughly investigated in assembled non-aq. Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2/MWCNT//Na cells, and showed higher specific capacity (over 100 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.15C) and had more stable cycle performance than those of the pristine Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2-based one.  It is noted that with increased charge-discharge cycles, the specific capacity of Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2/MWCNT gets close to the theor. capacity (ca. 117.4 mA h g-1).  These good performances could be attributed to the incorporated MWCNTs, which improve the cond. for lower charge transfer resistance and shorten the diffusion length for faster Na+ diffusion to access the reaction sites.  Through systematic studies of EIS at different states of charge and discharge, it is discovered that Rct decreases with the increase of voltage and reaches a min. value at redox sites, but Re and DNa+ show the opposite trend.  Moreover, a full cell test using a carbon black neg. electrode also demonstrates good capacity retention up to 50 cycles and a reversible capacity of 145 mA h g-1 with the av. operation voltage of 2.8 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrx2mz9QOT6v7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li9kfH2EjMgOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFWjtbbI&amp;md5=2cc7d2ba7d9b1d3de40ef1b912fb2ed0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA09403H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lin, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Deng, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding the effect of depressing surface moisture sensitivity on promoting sodium intercalation in coral-like Na<sub>3.12</sub>Fe<sub>2.44</sub>(P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>)<sub>2</sub>/C synthesized via a flash-combustion strategy</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2550</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2559</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the effect of depressing surface moisture sensitivity on promoting sodium intercalation in coral-like Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2/C synthesized via a flash-combustion strategy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin, Bo; Zhang, Sen; Deng, Chao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2550-2559</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The low-cost sodium iron pyrophosphate Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2, which enables facile ion transport, presents a promising alternative for use as the cathode of sodium ion batteries.  However, high moisture sensitivity and severe surface oxidn. lead to a large irreversible capacity and inferior electrochem. kinetics.  Herein, for the first time, we report the design of an ultrafast "flash-combustion synthesis" strategy to prep. coral-like Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2/C with good surface properties and fast sodium intercalation.  The single-phase Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2 is successfully prepd. in as short a time as three minutes.  Each ultrafine Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2 particle with a nanoscale carbon coating is enwrapped in a microscale carbon matrix, forming a coral-like architecture.  Benefiting from the hierarchical carbon decoration, the coral-like composite attains good surface properties that enable low moisture sensitivity and fast sodium intercalation.  Moreover, dynamic anal. reveals that surface oxidn. proceeds through a "shell-core" mechanism and demonstrates the crucial role of the surface properties on sodium intercalation.  Taking advantage of the good surface properties and the hierarchical porous architecture, the coral-like composite is capable of fast sodium intercalation and stable prolonged cycling.  It retains 95% of the initial capacity after 200 cycles alternating between 20 and 5C rates.  The clarification of the correlation between the surface properties and the sodium intercalation chem. provides clues to the design and construction of high-performance Na3.12Fe2.44(P2O7)2 for large-scale applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6Nnr0fqL-27Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li9kfH2EjMgOA"> &gt;&gt; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">;                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Study of the Crystal Structures of Sodium Magnesium and Sodium Nickel Diphosphates</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Erragh, Fatima; Boukhari, Ali; Abraham, Francis; Elouadi, Brahim</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2000</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">152</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">323-331</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JSSCBI</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0022-4596</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Academic Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Single-crystal x-ray crystallog. studies showed that diphosphates Na3.64Mg2.18(P2O7)2 and Na3.64Ni2.18(P2O7)2 crystallize with the same structural type and the same space group P‾1.  Their triclinic lattice parameters are a 10.901(2), b 9.765(2), c 6.382(1) Å, α 112.43(1), β 99.64(1), γ 107.53(1)°, Z = 2 and a 10.889(5), b 9.705(4), c 6.358(4) Å, α 112.46(4), β 99.92(4), γ 107.54(4)°, Z = 2, resp.  The structure could be regarded as a packing of diphosphate groups [P2O7]4- and [MO6] octahedra (M = Mg, Ni) delimiting cavities and tunnels which host Na cations.  The tunnels are running along [001].  The structure is characterized by mixed (Na,M) sites with an occupation factor ratio equal to ∼0.82/0.18.  Na cations are located in five different sites: two cavities (one penta- and the other octacoordinated) totally occupied and three octahedral interstices, which are partially filled by Na(3), Na(4), and Na(5) according to the resp. occupation factors of 0.15, 0.42, and 0.25 for Na3.64Mg2.18(P2O7)2 and 0.13, 0.40, and 0.29 in the case of Na3.64Ni2.18(P2O7)2.  (c) 2000 Academic Press.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoE39ebguKCBbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljNAI9FfqZTAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3cXktVKrsb4%253D&amp;md5=8b85b749bd43af26b6a62d1df9279cae</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.7b00196"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kotobuki, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.-D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Y-Doped Na<sub>2</sub>ZrO<sub>3</sub>: A Na-Rich Layered Oxide as a High-Capacity Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Sustainable Chem.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Y-Doped Na2ZrO3: A Na-Rich Layered Oxide as a High-Capacity Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Shufeng; Kotobuki, Masashi; Zheng, Feng; Xu, Chaohe; Hu, Ning; Lu, Li; Wang, Yu; Li, Wei-Dong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Sustainable Chemistry &amp; Engineering</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4785-4792</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASCECG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2168-0485</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The renewed interest in sodium-ion batteries reflects the persistent concern about the lithium resources that have widespread applications but an uneven distribution, and the overwhelming need for large-scale energy storage.  Most exploration has focused on the conventional layered oxides NaxMO2 that stem from lithium-ion cathodes.  However, exploring cathode materials with high capacities, long cycle lives, and low costs because of the large ionic radius and high at. wt. of sodium is a great challenge.  Here we report a Na-rich layered oxide, yttrium-doped Na2ZrO3, that serves as a cathode material in sodium-ion batteries.  This material delivers a large reversible capacity of ∼180 mAh g-1 and a good cycle life with no sign of obvious capacity decay over 1500 cycles along with a low cost.  The redox reactivity of oxygen is shown to be involved in the sodium extn.-insertion processes.  This work not only provides a cathode contender to conventional layered oxides NaxMO2 but also suggests that broad classes of defective Na-rich layered oxides could be discovered.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrImozRVdnnGrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljNAI9FfqZTAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXlvFOqsr0%253D&amp;md5=8c7c75c272aa02215fb93ac2519d2e34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/sia.1984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Grosvenor, A.-P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kobe, B.-A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Biesinger, M.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">McIntyre, N.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigation of multiplet splitting of Fe 2p XPS spectra and bonding in iron compounds</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Grosvenor, A. P.; Kobe, B. A.; Biesinger, M. C.; McIntyre, N. S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Surface and Interface Analysis</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2004</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ferrous (Fe2+) and ferric (Fe3+) compds. were studied by XPS to det. the usefulness of calcd. multiplet peaks to fit high-resoln. Fe 2p3/2 spectra from high-spin compds.  The multiplets fit most spectra well, particularly when contributions attributed to surface peaks and shake-up satellites were included.  This information was useful for fitting of the complex Fe 2p3/2 spectra for Fe3O4 where both Fe2+ and Fe3+ species are present.  As the ionic bond character of the Fe-ligand bond increased, the binding energy assocd. with either the ferrous or ferric 2p3/2 photoelectron peak increased.  This is due to the decrease in shielding of the Fe cation by the more increasingly electroneg. ligands.  Also the difference in energy between a high-spin Fe 2p3/2 peak and its corresponding shake-up satellite peak increased as the electronegativity of the ligand increased.  The extrinsic loss spectra for Fe oxides are reported; these are as characteristic of each species as are the photoelectron peaks.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqII9QNo6oMwLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljNAI9FfqZTAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXjtVWgtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=c71a7fc95f7cc23cc7b2de08dfb3b5c6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.apsusc.2007.09.063"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamashita, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hayes, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Analysis of XPS spectra of Fe<sup>2+</sup> and Fe<sup>3+</sup> ions in oxide materials</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Appl.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Analysis of XPS spectra of Fe2+ and Fe3+ ions in oxide materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yamashita, Toru; Hayes, Peter</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Samples of the iron oxides Fe0.94O, Fe3O4, Fe2O3, and Fe2SiO4 were prepd. by high temp. equilibration in controlled gas atmospheres.  The samples were fractured in vacuum and high resoln. XPS spectra of the fractured surfaces were measured.  The peak positions and peak shape parameters of Fe 3p for Fe2+ and Fe3+ were derived from the Fe 3p XPS spectra of the std. samples of 2FeO.SiO2 and Fe2O3, resp.  Using these parameters, the Fe 3p peaks of Fe3O4 and Fe1-yO were analyzed.  High resoln. XPS techniques can be used to det. the Fe2+/Fe3+ ratios in metal oxides.  The technique has the potential for application to other transition metal oxide systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqlqJbki4kamrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljNAI9FfqZTAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1cXhsVeltbk%253D&amp;md5=585b3b4682ffe8c9b48ec081207a07ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.ssc.2003.09.020"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Abbate, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ascolani, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Prado, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Caneiro, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electronic structure and band gap of the negative charge-transfer material Sr<sub>3</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub></span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Solid State Commun.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2004</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">129</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">113</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">116</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">10</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">74</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/nmat2920</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical investigation of the P2-NaxCoO2 phase diagram</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Berthelot, R.; Carlier, D.; Delmas, C.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">74-80</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na layered oxides NaxCoO2 form one of the most fascinating low-dimensional and strongly correlated systems; in particular P2-NaxCoO2 exhibits various single-phase domains with different Na+/vacancy patterns depending on the Na concn.  Here the authors used Na batteries to clearly depict the P2-NaxCoO2 phase diagram for x ≥ 0.50.  By coupling the electrochem. process with an in situ x-ray diffraction expt., the authors identified the succession of single-phase or two-phase domains appearing on Na intercalation with a rather good accuracy compared with previous studies.  The authors reported new single-phase domains and the authors underlined the thermal instability of some ordered phases from an electrochem. study at various temps.  As each phase was characterized by the position of its Fermi level vs. the Na+/Na couple, the synthesis of each material, even in large amts., can be carried out electrochem.  The phys. properties of the as-prepd. Na1/2CoO2 and Na2/3CoO2 ordered phases were characterized and compared.  Electrochem. processes are an accurate route to precisely study in a continuous way such a complex system and provide a new way to synthesize materials with a very narrow existence range.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrk1JcT1P9myrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lii7znua9zjzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhsFKisrvJ&amp;md5=d9d06332c38e3009393054b672c767f7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201600275"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ni, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polyanion-Type Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Sci.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_elocation-id">1600275</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/advs.201600275</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polyanion-Type Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni Qiao; Bai Ying; Wu Feng; Wu Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1600275</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries, representative members of the post-lithium-battery club, are very attractive and promising for large-scale energy storage applications.  The increasing technological improvements in sodium-ion batteries (Na-ion batteries) are being driven by the demand for Na-based electrode materials that are resource-abundant, cost-effective, and long lasting.  Polyanion-type compounds are among the most promising electrode materials for Na-ion batteries due to their stability, safety, and suitable operating voltages.  The most representative polyanion-type electrode materials are Na3V2(PO4)3 and NaTi2(PO4)3 for Na-based cathode and anode materials, respectively.  Both show superior electrochemical properties and attractive prospects in terms of their development and application in Na-ion batteries.  Carbonophosphate Na3MnCO3PO4 and amorphous FePO4 have also recently emerged and are contributing to further developing the research scope of polyanion-type Na-ion batteries.  However, the typical low conductivity and relatively low capacity performance of such materials still restrict their development.  This paper presents a brief review of the research progress of polyanion-type electrode materials for Na-ion batteries, summarizing recent accomplishments, highlighting emerging strategies, and discussing the remaining challenges of such systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRzOrk04pyNfsjl5L8hwNX0fW6udTcc2ebiWRVs-AqDYrntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1cvgtVOitA%253D%253D&amp;md5=f4bc597b44df5e4e4c0b0a698c9a4d56</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1149/1.3555102"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Didier, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guignard, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Denage, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Szajwaj, O.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ito, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Saadoune, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Darriet, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Delmas, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Na-Deintercalation from NaVO<sub>2</sub></span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochem.                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical Na-Deintercalation from NaVO2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Didier, C.; Guignard, M.; Denage, C.; Szajwaj, O.; Ito, S.; Saadoune, I.; Darriet, J.; Delmas, C.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochemical and Solid-State Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A75-A78</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ESLEF6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1099-0062</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This paper describes the prepn. of NaxVO2 phases by electrochem. deintercalation.  The curves V = f(x) show that the process is reversible up to x = 0.5 and they indicate multiple single phase domains in the range 1 &lt; x &lt; 0.5.  Two single phases were successfully isolated for Na1/2VO2 and Na2/3VO2 compns.; the authors report here the 1st x-ray powder diffraction measurements of these phases.  They present a O'3-type monoclinic distortion of the O3 rhombohedral phase obsd. for Na1VO2.  The evolution of cell parameters with Na deintercalation is comparable with other AxMO2 layered oxides.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYtKHyy3LVlrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdDiwh-JL5dw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXivVGisrw%253D&amp;md5=f443243e7ccaf4e42e86f5a389bd437f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1016/S0167-2738(99)00145-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Blesa, M.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Moran, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Leo’n, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Santamaria, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tornero, J.-D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mene’ndez, N.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title"><i>a</i>-NaFeO: ionic conductivity and sodium extraction</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Solid State Ionics</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1999</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">126</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">81</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">87</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/S0167-2738(99)00145-9</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">α-NaFeO2: ionic conductivity and sodium extraction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Blesa, M. C.; Moran, E.; Leon, C.; Santamaria, J.; Tornero, J. D.; Menendez, N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Solid State Ionics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1999</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">126</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1,2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">81-87</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SSIOD3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0167-2738</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Complex admittance measurements have been performed on α-NaFeO2 and on the product Na0.9FeO2 obtained by sodium extn., both being polycryst. powders.  The elec. cond. in both samples is proposed to be due to sodium ions hopping between octahedral positions through the adjacent, empty, tetrahedral ones characteristic of a rock-salt structural framework.  The parent material shows an activation energy in the d.c. cond. of 0.31 eV between 306 and 498 K.  Removal of sodium, in spite of creating octahedral vacancies, results in lower cond. values, and a higher activation energy of 0.58 eV in a similar temp. range.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrNx6t7nnuGdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdDiwh-JL5dw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3cXhtVajsrw%253D&amp;md5=4d7b27b8f61e3790836bed3f60ca1d49</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1021/jp5105888"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ikeuchi, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nakayama, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Takei, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shiiba, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nakayama, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">New Insight into Structural Evolution in Layered NaCrO<sub>2</sub> during Electrochemical Sodium Extraction</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. properties and structural changes during charge for NaCrO2, whose structure is classified as α-NaFeO2 type layered polymorph (also O3-type following the Delmas' notation), were examd. as a pos. electrode material for nonaq.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a 3.8 V manganese-based mixed-phosphate cathode material for applications in sodium rechargeable batteries; i.e., Na4Mn3(PO4)2(P2O7).  This material exhibits a largest Mn2+/Mn3+ redox potential of 3.84 V vs.  Na+/Na yet reported for a manganese-based cathode, together with the largest energy d. of 416 W h kg-1.  We describe first-principles calcns. and exptl. results which show that three-dimensional Na diffusion pathways with low-activation-energy barriers enable the rapid sodium insertion and extn. at various states of charge of the Na4-xMn3(PO4)2(P2O7) electrode (where x = 0, 1, 3).  Furthermore, we show that the sodium ion mobility in this crystal structure is not decreased by the structural changes induced by Jahn-Teller distortion (Mn3+), in contrast to most manganese-based electrodes, rather it is increased due to distortion, which opens up sodium diffusion channels.  This feature stabilizes the material, providing high cycle stability and high power performance for sodium rechargeable batteries.  The high voltage, large energy d., cycle stability and the use of low-cost Mn give Na4Mn3(PO4)2(P2O7) significant potential for applications as a cathode material for large-scale Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqkGCBDNIeK6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgP5uyh2B4RNQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFWhtL%252FE&amp;md5=627f366282ae7d72c11a642edc8e90d4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201402095"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Barpanda, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, G.-D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Maxim, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamada, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">t-Na2(VO)P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>: A 3.8 V Pyrophosphate Insertion Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ChemElectroChem</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">1</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1488</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1491</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
